20:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:29:49","title":"Chrome 83 Beta: Cross-site Scripting Protection, Improved Form Controls, and Safe Cross-origin Resource Sharing","link":"http://blog.chromium.org/2020/04/chrome-83-beta-cross-site-scripting.html","description":"Unless otherwise noted, changes described below apply to the newest Chrome beta channel release for Android, Chrome OS, Linux, macOS, and Windows. Learn more about the features listed here through the provided links or from the list on <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features#milestone%3D76\">ChromeStatus.com</a>. Chrome 83 is beta as of April 16, 2020.<br /><h1>Trusted Types for DOM Manipulation</h1>DOM-based cross-site scripting (DOM XSS) is one of the most common web security vulnerabilities. It can even be introduced to your application unintentionally. Trusted types is a new technology that helps you write and maintain applications that are free of DOM XSS vulnerabilities by default. It does this by securing dangerous APIs. <br /><br />Consider a property like <code><a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Element/innerHTML\">Element.innerHTML</a></code>. This property can open your site to harmful HTML manipulation. Trusted types would cause your script to throw an error if this property were used. To do this, set a new content security policy. For example:<br /><br /><br /><pre>Content-Security-Policy: require-trusted-types-for 'script';<br />report-uri //my-csp-endpoint.example<br /></pre><br /><br />For more information on trusted types, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/trusted-types/\">Prevent DOM-based cross-site scripting vulnerabilities with Trusted Types</a>.<br /><h1>Improved Form Controls</h1>HTML form controls provide the backbone for much of the web's interactivity. They're easy for developers to use, have built-in accessibility, and are familiar to our users. Unfortunately, the styling of form controls is wildly inconsistent. The earliest form controls matched the operating system on which they displayed, and later controls followed whatever design style was popular at the time they were created. This variation forced developers to spend extra time in development and to ship extra code. <br /><br />Over the last year, Chrome and Edge have collaborated to improve the appearance and function of HTML form controls. This work included making the focused states of controls and other interactive elements easier to perceive. The images below show the old and new versions of some controls in Chrome. <br /><br />The old versions:<br /><span id=\"docs-internal-guid-efc726bf-7fff-1158-6a6c-b92174f349f4\"><span style=\"font-family: arial; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"border: none; display: inline-block; height: 560px; overflow: hidden; width: 297px;\"><img height=\"560\" src=\"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/Yrw-54mhu6WWPdl5pI9dEmZt2rHeo7YQDmRD9mvGfUHIFwtszRY_Lfa4KDdypM7fbxRDkceoHsXAbPhw4mz9dCZtSPDnJJDdaF2YWdZ05NNbHXDD98NLtUJ4W3tkYTT9SSOQO3M8\" style=\"margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;\" width=\"297\" /><b></b></span></span></span><br /><br />The new versions:<br /><span id=\"docs-internal-guid-30a4ef93-7fff-58a6-0dce-267d6c3c7978\"><span style=\"font-family: arial; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"border: none; display: inline-block; height: 522px; overflow: hidden; width: 277px;\"><img height=\"522\" src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/WLjG9k0ctIUOfJai0QqFBqxXy5TdoS06q6_mcwJYzqcu5TATgTjAkzEKpf7m8of5ymdwR9QKI1SSFOs31ubDTr5M5pcN1T7TWpFn2N766VG31dk0JibAMMlt-ChNNgFg1f6IfAqK\" style=\"margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;\" width=\"277\" /></span></span></span><br />The new form controls have already shipped in Microsoft Edge and are now available in Chrome 83. For more information see Microsoft's article <a href=\"https://blogs.windows.com/msedgedev/2019/10/15/form-controls-microsoft-edge-chromium/\">Improving form controls in Microsoft Edge and Chromium</a> or our post on the Chromium blog <a href=\"https://blog.chromium.org/2020/03/updates-to-form-controls-and-focus.html\">Updates to Form Controls and Focus</a>.<br /><br /><h1>New Cross-Origin Policies</h1>Some web APIs increase the risk of side-channel attacks like Spectre. To mitigate that risk, browsers offer an opt-in-based isolated environment called cross-origin isolated. This is done through two new HTTP headers: <code>Cross-Origin-Embedder-Policy</code><br />and  <code>Cross-Origin-Opener-Policy</code>. With these headers, web pages can safely use privileged features including:<br /><ul><li><code>Performance.measureMemory()</code></li><li>JS Self-Profiling API</li></ul>The cross-origin isolated state also prevents modifications of <code>document.domain</code>. <br /><br /><span id=\"docs-internal-guid-8f6c2368-7fff-9edd-44d7-b09e85086324\"></span><br />For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/coop-coep/\">Making your website \"cross-origin isolated\" using COOP and COEP</a>.<br /><h1>Origin Trials</h1>This version of Chrome introduces the origin trials described below. Origin trials allow you to try new features and give feedback on usability, practicality, and effectiveness to the web standards community. To register for any of the origin trials currently supported in Chrome, including the ones described below, visit the <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/trials/active\">Origin Trials dashboard</a>. To learn more about origin trials themselves, visit the <a href=\"https://github.com/GoogleChrome/OriginTrials/blob/gh-pages/developer-guide.md\">Origin Trials Guide for Web Developers</a>.<br /><br /><h2>Native File System</h2>The Native File System API is in a new origin trial, scheduled to run from Chrome 83 to Chrome 85. This API enables developers to build web apps that interact with files on the user's local device such as IDEs, photo and video editors, text editors, and more. After a user grants access, the API lets apps read or save changes directly to files and folders on the user's device. It does this by invoking the platform's own open and save dialog boxes.  For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/native-file-system/\">The Native File System API: Simplifying access to local files</a>.<br /><br /><h2>Performance.measureMemory()</h2>The new <code>Performance.measureMemory()</code> function estimates the memory usage of a web page to measure the memory usage of a web app or page in production. The use cases include:<br /><ul><li>Analysis of correlation between memory usage and user metrics</li><li>Detection of memory regressions</li><li>Evaluation of feature launches in A/B tests</li><li>Memory optimization. </li></ul>Currently web developers resort to the non-standard performance.memory API that is used in 20% of page loads. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/monitor-total-page-memory-usage/\">Monitor your web page's total memory usage with performance.measureMemory()</a>.<br /><br /><h2>Prioritized Scheduler.postTask()</h2>The <code><a href=\"https://chromestatus.com/feature/6031161734201344\">Scheduler.postTask()</a></code> method allows developers to schedule tasks (javascript callbacks) with a native browser scheduler at three levels of priority: <code>user-blocking</code>, <code>user-visible</code>, and <code>background</code>. It also exposes a <code>TaskController</code> object, which can be used to dynamically cancel tasks and change their priority.<br /><br /><h2>WebRTC Insertable Streams</h2>The <a href=\"https://github.com/alvestrand/webrtc-media-streams/blob/master/explainer.md\">WebRTC Insertable Streams API</a> lets applications provide custom data processing in the encoding and decoding of a WebRTC <code><a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/MediaStreamTrack\">MediaStreamTrack</a></code>&nbsp;One use case for this is the end-to-end encryption of the data transferred between peer connections via an intermediate server. To use insertable streams add one of the new parameters to the <code><a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/RTCPeerConnection/RTCPeerConnection\">RTCPeerConnection</a>&nbsp;</code>interface. Other WebRTC updates in the release are listed in the next section.<br /><h1>Other features in this release</h1><h2>ARIA Annotations</h2><a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/4666935918723072\">New ARIA annotations</a> support screen reader accessibility for comments, suggestions, and text highlights with semantic meanings (similar to <code>&lt;mark&gt;</code>). Additionally, related information can now be tied semantically to an element allowing descriptions, definitions, footnotes and comments to be tied to another element.<br />Annotations were not previously possible without resorting to live region hacks, which are not as reliable as semantics, and do not work well with braille displays. As a result, screen reader users have non-optimal support for collaboration features of online word processors.<br /><br /><h2>'auto' keyword for '-webkit-appearance' CSS property</h2>The <code>-webkit-appearance </code>CSS property has <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5913213940006912\">a new <code>auto</code> keyword</a>, which indicates the default appearance of the target element. This is a step on the way towards replacing the non-standard <code>-webkit-appearance</code> property with a future fully standardized <code>appearance</code> property. <br /><br /><h2>Barcode Detection API</h2>Chrome now supports the Barcode Detection API, a subset of the Shape Detection API which provides the ability to detect and decode barcodes in an image provided by a script. The image may come from any type of image buffer source such as an <code>&lt;image&gt;</code>, <code>&lt;video&gt;</code> or <code>&lt;canvas&gt;</code> tag. Previously supporting barcode detection on  a web page required inclusion of a large third-party library. This API is only available on devices with <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.google.android.gms\">Google Play Services</a> installed and is not available on uncertified devices. For information about the Barcode Detection API as well as the other Shape Detection APIs, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/shape-detection/\">The Shape Detection API: a picture is worth a thousand words, faces, and barcodes</a>.<br /><br /><h2>CSS Color Adjust: color-scheme meta tag</h2>Many operating systems now have a \"dark mode\" preference. Some browsers already offer an option to transform web pages into a dark theme. The <code>prefers-color-scheme</code> media query lets authors support their own dark theme so they have full control over experiences they build. The meta tag lets a site explicitly opt-in to fully supporting a dark theme so that the browser loads a different user agent sheet and not ever apply transformations. For more information, read <a href=\"https://web.dev/color-scheme/\">Improved dark mode default styling with the color-scheme CSS property and the corresponding meta tag</a>.<br /><br /><h2>display:inline-grid/grid/inline-flex/flex for &lt;button&gt;</h2>The <code>display</code> keywords <code>inline-grid</code>, <code>grid</code>, <code>inline-flex</code>, and <code>flex</code> <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5213452823953408\">now function with the <code>&lt;button&gt;</code> element</a> when the align property is applied. (<a href=\"https://codepen.io/jpmedley/pen/MWwmoQE\">Demo</a>)<br /><br /><h2>ES Modules for shared workers ('module' type option)</h2>JavaScript now supports modules in shared workers. Setting <code>module</code> type by the constructor's type attribute, worker scripts are loaded as ES modules and the import statement is available in worker contexts. With this feature, web developers can more easily write programs in a composable way and share them among a page and workers. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/module-workers/#what-about-shared-workers\">What about shared workers</a> in Threading the web with module workers.<br /><br /><h2>Improvements to font-display: optional</h2>A few changes have been made to the way <code>font-display</code> works on Chrome.<br /><ul><li>Setting <code>font-display</code> to <code>optional</code> no longer causes relayout</li><li>Web font preloading is allowed to slightly block rendering (for all <code>font-display</code> values), so that if the font loads fast enough, we don't need to render with fallback.</li></ul>Consequently, when <code>font-display: optional</code> and preloading are used together, you'll never see layout shifting from font swapping. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/preload-optional-fonts/\">Prevent layout shifting and flashes of invisibile text (FOIT) by preloading optional fonts</a>.<br /><br /><h2>IndexedDB relaxed durability transactions</h2><code><a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5730701489995776\">IDBDatabase.transaction()</a></code> now accepts an optional <code>durability</code> argument<br />to control flushing of data to storage. This allows developers to explicitly trade off durability for performance. Previously after writing an IndexedDB transaction, Firefox did not flush to disk but Chrome did. This provided increased durability by guaranteeing that data is written to the device's disk rather than merely to an intermediate OS cache. Unfortunately, this comes with a significant performance cost.   <br />Valid options are <code>\"default\"</code>, <code>\"strict\"</code>, and <code>\"relaxed\"</code>. The <code>\"default\"</code> option uses whatever behavior is provided by the user agent and is currently the default. An example is shown below. The current value may be read using <code>IDBTransaction.durability</code>.<br /><br /><pre>const iDBTransaction = database.transaction(<br />&nbsp; [ \"storeName\" ],<br />&nbsp; \"readwrite\",<br />&nbsp; {<br />&nbsp; &nbsp; durability: \"relaxed\"<br />&nbsp; }<br />);</pre><br /><br /><h2>Out-Of-Renderer Cross-Origin Resource Sharing</h2>Out-Of-Renderer Cross-Origin Resource Sharing (OOR-CORS) is a new CORS implementation that inspects network accesses. Chrome's previous CORS implementation was only available to Blink core parts, XHR and Fetch APIs, while a simplified implementation was used in other parts of the application. HTTP requests made by some internal modules could not be inspected for CORS at all. The new implementation addresses these shortcomings.<br /><br /><h2>Reversed range for &lt;input type=time&gt;</h2>Chrome <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5347108783652864\">now supports reversed ranges for <code>&lt;input&gt;</code> elements</a> whose <code>type</code> is <code>time</code>, allowing developers to express time inputs that cross midnight. A reversed range is one where the maximum is less than the minimum. In this state, the input allows values that are less than the minimum or greater than the maximum, but not between them. This functionality has been in the specification for many years, but has not yet been implemented in Chrome. <br /><br /><h2>Support \"JIS-B5\" and \"JIS-B4\" @page</h2>Chrome <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5112328557166592\">now supports two page sizes for the @page rule</a>, both listed in the CSS Paged Media Module Level 3 spec.<br /><ul><li>\"JIS-B5\": 182mm wide by 257mm high</li><li>\"JIS-B4\": 257mm wide by 364mm high</li></ul>This feature completes Chrome's implementation of this section of the standard.<br /><br /><h2>@supports selector() feature query function</h2>The new <code>@supports</code> function provides <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5555643303854080\">feature detection for CSS selectors</a>. Web authors can use this feature to query whether the UA supports the selector before they actually try to apply the specified style rules matching the selector. For example:<br /><br /><pre>@supports selector(::before) {<br />  div { background: green };<br />}</pre><h2>WebRTC</h2>Chrome has added the following web RTC features in addition to the one already mention under Origin Trials.<br /><h3>RTCPeerConnection.canTrickleIceCandidates</h3>The <code><a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/6222269451862016\">canTrickleIceCandidates</a></code> boolean property indicates whether a remote peer is capable of handling trickle candidates. It exposes information from the SDP session description.<br /><br /><h3>RTCRtpEncodingParameters.maxFramerate</h3><a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/6216116758118400\">This encoding parameter</a> allows developers to limit the framerate on a video layer before sending. Use <code>RTCRtpSender.setParameters()</code> to set the new framerate, which takes effect after the current picture is complete. read it back using <code>RTCRtpEncodingParameters.maxFramerate</code>. Setting <code>maxFramerate</code> to 0 freezes the video on the next frame.<br /><br /><h3>RTCRtpSendParameters.degradationPreference</h3>A new attribute for <code>RTCRtpSendParameters</code> called <code>degradationPreference</code> allows developers to control how quality degrades when constraints such as bandwidth or CPU prevent encoding at the configured frame rate and resolution. For example, on a screen share app, users will probably prefer screen legibility over animations. On a video conference users likely prefer a smooth frame rate over a higher resolution. Valid values for <code>degradationPreference</code> are <code>\"maintain-framerate\"</code>,  <code>\"maintain-resolution\"</code>, and <code>\"balanced\"</code>.<br /><br /><h2>WebXR DOM Overlay</h2>DOM overlay is a feature for immersive AR on handheld devices that lets two-dimensional page content be shown as an interactive transparent layer on top of the WebXR content and camera image. With this feature, developers can use the DOM to create user interfaces for WebXR experiences. For VR, inline sessions are by definition within the DOM. For AR, though, there is no inline mode making this particularly important for certain use cases. To try the feature use one of the <a href=\"https://klausw.github.io/a-frame-car-sample/index.html\">two</a> <a href=\"https://klausw.github.io/three.js/examples/webvr_lorenzattractor.html\">samples</a> in Chrome 83. This feature is currently only available on ARCore-based handheld devices.<br /><br /><h1>JavaScript</h1>This version of Chrome incorporates version 8.3 of the V8 JavaScript engine. It specifically includes the changes listed below. You can find a complete <a href=\"https://v8.dev/blog\">list of recent features</a> in the V8 release notes.<br /><h2>fractionalSecondDigits option for Intl.DateTimeFormat</h2>Chrome 83 <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5704965743968256\">adds the <code>fractionalSecondDigits</code> property</a> to the <code>Intl.DateTimeFormat</code> object to control the format of fractions of a second. The Date object in ECMAScript stores time information with millisecond precision, which some web developers need to output. The value of this property is an integer between 0 and 3 to represent how many digits the <code>DateTimeFormat</code> should output after the decimal mark.<br /><h1>Deprecations, and Removals</h1>This version of Chrome introduces the deprecations and removals listed below. Visit ChromeStatus.com for lists of <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features#browsers.chrome.status%3A%22Deprecated%22\">current deprecations</a>  and <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features#browsers.chrome.status:%22Removed%22\">previous removals</a>.<br /><h2>Disallow Downloads in Sandboxed iframes</h2>Chrome now <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5706745674465280\">prevents downloads in sandboxed iframes</a>, though this restriction can be lifted via an <code>'allow-downloads'</code> keyword in the sandbox attribute list. This allows content providers to restrict malicious or abusive downloads. Downloads can bring security vulnerabilities to a system. Even though additional security checks are done in Chrome and the operating system, we feel blocking downloads in sandboxed iframes also fits the purpose of the sandbox.<br /><br /><span class=\"post-author\">Posted by Joe Medley</span>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 17 Apr 2020 14:41:00 +0000","feedId":649,"bgimg":"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/Yrw-54mhu6WWPdl5pI9dEmZt2rHeo7YQDmRD9mvGfUHIFwtszRY_Lfa4KDdypM7fbxRDkceoHsXAbPhw4mz9dCZtSPDnJJDdaF2YWdZ05NNbHXDD98NLtUJ4W3tkYTT9SSOQO3M8","linkMd5":"60b73d2b1f9134bd4086dec427660b20","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn14@2020_2/2020/08/16/12-29-50-223_7e0b1827fab54716.webp","destWidth":492,"destHeight":928,"author":"Chromium Blog","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/Yrw-54mhu6WWPdl5pI9dEmZt2rHeo7YQDmRD9mvGfUHIFwtszRY_Lfa4KDdypM7fbxRDkceoHsXAbPhw4mz9dCZtSPDnJJDdaF2YWdZ05NNbHXDD98NLtUJ4W3tkYTT9SSOQO3M8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn1@2020_2/2020/08/16/12-29-51-588_7e0b1827fab54716.webp","https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/WLjG9k0ctIUOfJai0QqFBqxXy5TdoS06q6_mcwJYzqcu5TATgTjAkzEKpf7m8of5ymdwR9QKI1SSFOs31ubDTr5M5pcN1T7TWpFn2N766VG31dk0JibAMMlt-ChNNgFg1f6IfAqK":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn97@2020_5/2020/08/16/12-29-50-250_8217febe5604d986.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 20:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 20:29:49","title":"Chrome 85: Upload Streaming, Human Interface Devices, Custom Properties with Inheritance and More","link":"http://blog.chromium.org/2020/07/chrome-85-upload-streaming-human.html","description":"<p>Unless otherwise noted, changes described below apply to the newest Chrome beta channel release for Android, Chrome OS, Linux, macOS, and Windows. Learn more about the features listed here through the provided links or from the list on <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features#milestone%3D76\">ChromeStatus.com</a>. Chrome 85 is beta as of July 23, 2020.</p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">Fetch Upload Streaming </h2>\n<p>Fetch upload streaming lets web developers make a fetch with a <a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/ReadableStream\"><font face=\"courier\">ReadableStream</font></a> body. Starting in Chrome 85, it's <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/view_trial/-7680889164480380927\">available for an origin trial</a>.</p> \n<p>Previously, you could only start a request once you had the whole body ready to go. But now, you can start sending data while you're still generating the content, improving performance and memory usage.</p> \n<p>For example, an online form could initiate a fetch as soon as a user focuses a text input field. By the time the user clicks enter, <font face=\"courier\">fetch()</font> headers would already have been sent. This feature also allows you to send content as it's generated on the client, such as audio and video. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/fetch-upload-streaming\">Streaming requests with the fetch API</a>.</p> \n<p>See the <a href=\"http://blog.chromium.org/2020/07/chrome-85-upload-streaming-human.html#origin-trials\">Origin Trials section</a> for information on signing up and for a list of other origin trials starting in this release. This origin trial is expected to run through Chrome 87 in January 2021.</p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">WebHID API</h2>\n<p>There is a long tail of human interface devices (HIDs) that are too new, too old, or too uncommon to be accessible by systems' device drivers. The WebHID API solves this by providing a way to implement device-specific logic in JavaScript. In Chrome 85, it's available <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/view_trial/1074108511127863297\">for an origin trial</a>.</p> \n<p>An HID is one that takes input from or provides output to humans. Examples of devices include keyboards, pointing devices (mice, touchscreens, etc.), and gamepads. </p> \n<p>The inability to access uncommon or unusual HID devices is particularly painful when it comes to gamepad support. Gamepad inputs and outputs are not well standardized and web browsers often require custom logic for specific devices. This is unsustainable and results in poor support for the long tail of older and uncommon devices. </p> \n<p>We're working on an article to show you how to use the new API. In the meantime, we've found some demos from a few eager engineers that you can use to try the new API. To see those demos, check out <a href=\"https://web.dev/hid-examples/\">Human interface devices on the web: a few quick examples</a>.</p> \n<p>See the <a href=\"http://blog.chromium.org/2020/07/chrome-85-upload-streaming-human.html#origin-trials\">Origin Trials section</a> for information on signing up and for a list of other origin trials starting in this release. This origin trial is expected to run through Chrome 87 in January 2021.</p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">Windows Support for getInstalledRelatedApps()</h2>\n<p>The <font face=\"courier\">navigator.getInstalledRelatedApps()</font> method determines whether a site's corresponding native app is installed. This allows customization of a user experience for already-installed apps. For example, users can be redirected from a product marketing page directly into an app. Functionality can be centralized to prevent users from seeing duplicate notifications and save developers from maintaining two code bases. Sites can even avoid prompting for installation of a PWA if a native app is already on a user's device.</p> \n<p>It does all this while protecting user privacy. Entries in the web app manifest and the Android manifest file ensure that sites cannot use the API to request arbitrary information about users' installed apps.</p> \n<p>This method was implemented on Android in Chrome 80. Starting in Chrome 85, it's available on Microsoft Windows. This addition is the result of work from Microsoft. For details on using this method, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/get-installed-related-apps/\">Is your app installed? getInstalledRelatedApps() will tell you!</a>.</p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">@property</h2>\n<p>CSS Houdini is a <a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/Houdini#The_Houdini_APIs\">set of APIs and CSS features</a> that exposes the CSS rendering engine. It lets developers create new CSS features without waiting for a native implementation in browsers. CSS Houdini's <font face=\"courier\">@property</font> rule is part of the <a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/CSS_Properties_and_Values_API\">CSS Properties and Values API</a>, which allows defining custom properties with inheritance, type checking, and default values. The first part of this API, <a href=\"https://web.dev/css-props-and-vals/\"><font face=\"courier\">CSS.registerProperty()</font>, was implemented in Chrome 78</a>. That method's capabilities are now available in stylesheets through the <font face=\"courier\">@property</font>.</p> \n<p>Take the image below, for example. What you're seeing is a transition created with a CSS custom property. In addition to being impossible without the new API, this transition is also type safe. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/at-property/\">@property: giving superpowers to CSS variables</a>.</p>\n<p><span id=\"docs-internal-guid-3bde3d91-7fff-e4d7-3b24-c2a7584c4e7d\"><span style=\"font-family: arial; font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"border: none; display: inline-block; height: 235px; overflow: hidden; width: 624px;\"><img height=\"235\" src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/_9-HI9MJm8ceOq7KAufk0iA2q-KZRifd2TYY22XdjVEIefm6Vu_hJ3XLePtbDna3nPwkrnczbkxVAEs9L7EygV4RGpT8LtMYHn6iPKgHHoxLxvll5TShDPV2OV39fUnDVJzzEq_zCg\" style=\"margin-left: 0px; margin-top: 0px;\" width=\"624\" /></span></span></span></p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\"><a name=\"origin-trials\"></a>Origin Trials</h2>\n<p>In addition to those listed above, this version of Chrome introduces the new origin trials described below. Origin trials allow you to try new features and give feedback on usability, practicality, and effectiveness to the web standards community. To register for any of the origin trials currently supported in Chrome, including the ones described below, visit the <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/trials/active\">Origin Trials dashboard</a>. To learn more about origin trials themselves, visit the <a href=\"https://github.com/GoogleChrome/OriginTrials/blob/gh-pages/developer-guide.md\">Origin Trials Guide for Web Developers</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">New Origin Trials</h3> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: left;\">Declarative Shadow DOM</h4>\n<p>A <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5191745052606464\">declarative API</a> to allow the creation of shadow roots using only HTML and no JavaScript. This API allows Web Components that use Shadow DOM to also make use of server-side rendering (SSR), to get rendered content on screen quickly without requiring JavaScript for shadow root attachment. The origin trial is expected to <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/view_trial/2024368032503037953\">run through Chrome 87</a> in January 2020.</p> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: left;\">RTCRtpEncodingParameters.adaptivePtime Property</h4>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5752004691361792\"><font face=\"courier\">RTCRtpEncodingParameters.adaptivePtime</font> property</a> lets a sender in a real-time communication (RTC) system enable or disable adaptive packet rates. Because the packet rate is a big determining factor to the overall bitrate of an audio stream, an optimal congestion control is needed to adapt the packet rate. The audio packet rate is analogous to the video frame rate, which also plays an important role in the video bitrate adaptation.<br /><br />Although adaptive packet rate may be ubiquitously beneficial, we need this API for applications to enable and disable it, since, otherwise, it may introduce interoperability problems. Some implementations have taken a fixed packet rate as an assumption, and thus may fail or perform sub-optimally with an adaptive packet rate. The origin trial is expected to <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/register_trial/3163778738227773441\">run through Chrome 87</a> in January 2021.</p> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: left;\">Portals</h4>\n<p>Portals enable seamless navigations between sites or pages by allowing a page to show another page as an inset. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/hands-on-portals/\">Hands-on with Portals: seamless navigation on the Web</a>. The origin trial is expected to <a href=\"https://developers.chrome.com/origintrials/#/view_trial/-7680889164480380927\">run through Chrome 86</a> in early November.</p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">Other Features in this Release</h2> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">App Shortcuts</h3>\n<p>App shortcuts are now available on desktop in addition to Android, which debuted in Chrome 84. This feature improves users' productivity and facilitates reengagement with key tasks by providing quick access to common actions. For sites that are already Progressive Web Apps, creating shortcuts requires only adding items to the web app manifest. This addition is the result of work from Microsoft. For more information, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/app-shortcuts/\">Get things done quickly with app shortcuts</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Autoupgrade Mixed Content</h3>\n<p>Chrome is now <a href=\"https://chromestatus.com/feature/5557268741357568\">auto-upgrading images</a> served over HTTP from HTTPS sites by rewriting URLs to HTTPS without falling back to HTTP when secure content is not available. Chrome has been auto-upgrading audio and video content since version 80.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">AVIF Image Decode</h3>\n<p>Adds <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/4905307790639104\">support for decoding AVIF content</a> natively using existing AV1 decoders. AVIF is a next generation image format standardized by the <a href=\"https://aomedia.org/\">Alliance for Open Media</a>. There are three primary motivations for supporting AVIF:</p>\n<ul>\n <li>Reducing bandwidth consumption to load pages faster and reduce overall data consumption. AVIF offers significant file size reduction for images compared with JPEG or WebP. </li>\n <li>Adding HDR color support. AVIF is a path to HDR image support for the web. JPEG is limited in practice to 8-bit color depth. With displays increasingly capable of higher brightness, color bit depth, and color gamuts, web stakeholders are increasingly interested in preserving image data that is lost with JPEG.</li>\n <li>Supporting ecosystem interest. Companies with a large web presence have expressed an interest in shipping AVIF images on the web. </li>\n</ul> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Changes to Persistent Storage for Installed Web Apps</h3>\n<p>Getting <a href=\"https://web.dev/persistent-storage/\">persistent storage</a> is easier and more predictable for installed web apps, including PWAs and Trusted Web Activities. If an installed web app requests persistent storage by calling <code>navigator.storage.persist()</code>, it will be granted automatically. Other sites will continue to use the existing <a href=\"https://web.dev/persistent-storage/#chrome-and-other-chromium-based-browsers\">heuristics</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">CSS</h3> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: left;\">Color Adjust: Remove 'only' and Support 'dark' or 'light' for color-scheme”</h4>\n<p>Chrome made <a href=\"https://www.blogger.com/blog/post/edit/2471378914199150966/8521804084878530634\">two changes</a> to match those made in the CSS Color Adjustment level 1 spec.</p>\n<ul>\n <li>The <font face=\"courier\">'only'</font> keyword is no longer special and is treated as a <font face=\"courier\">&lt;custom-ident&gt;</font> as any other unknown color-scheme. The <font face=\"courier\">'only'</font> keyword was previously only allowed in combination with <font face=\"courier\">'light'</font>, but had otherwise no effect in Chrome.</li>\n <li>Page authors can now use dark-themed UA rendering even when the preferred color-scheme is 'light'. The new behavior is:\n  <ul>\n   <li>color-scheme: light -&gt; always light</li>\n   <li>color-scheme: dark -&gt; always dark</li>\n   <li>color-scheme: light dark -&gt; select the preferred scheme</li>\n  </ul></li>\n</ul>\n<p>This means content which has a dark theme in its CSS will be able to match it with dark themed UA controls.<br /><br />This change improves interoperability with WebKit which already had this behavior for <font face=\"courier\">'color-scheme: dark'</font>.</p> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: left;\">content-visibility Property</h4>\n<p>Adds a CSS property called <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/4613920211861504\"><font face=\"courier\">content-visibility</font></a>, which allows automatic or script management of content visibility. When hidden, the element's contents (subtree or replaced element contents) are not drawn or hit-tested and have CSS containment applied, allowing for rendering optimizations. The <font face=\"courier\">'auto'</font> keyword allows for the user-agent to manage content visibility based on proximity to the viewport, whereas the <font face=\"courier\">'hidden'</font> keyword allows full script control of content visibility.</p> \n<h4 style=\"text-align: left;\">counter-set</h4>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/4688138070917120\">CSS <font face=\"courier\">counter-set</font></a> is an additional property introduced in <a href=\"https://drafts.csswg.org/css-lists-3/\">CSS Lists Module Level 3</a> to control counters by setting an existing counter to a specified value. This builds on other implemented counter control properties, specifically counter-reset (which creates a new counter with a specified value) and counter-increment (which increments an existing counter by a specified amount). This feature is needed for precise counter control, since otherwise it is not possible to set an existing counter to a value other than figuring out how to increment or decrement it.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Event Timing API</h3>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features/5167290693713920\">Event Timing API</a> enables web developers to measure event latency both before and after the page load. Monitoring event latency requires an event listener. This precludes measuring event latency early in page load, and adds unnecessary performance overhead.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Expose Picture-in-Picture Window in leavepictureinpicture event</h3>\n<p>(Desktop only) The <font face=\"courier\">leavepictureinpicture</font> event <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5719215132639232\">now exposes a reference to <font face=\"courier\">pictureInPictureWindow</font></a> so that web developers no longer need to keep a global reference to that object.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Named pages with page-orientation</h3>\n<p>Support is added for <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5173237715566592\">several CSS properties</a> and descriptors for printing.</p>\n<ul>\n <li>The <font face=\"courier\">'page'</font> CSS property.</li>\n <li>Named pages. For example: <font face=\"courier\">@page foobar {}</font></li>\n <li>The <font face=\"courier\">'page-orientation'</font> descriptor with values <font face=\"courier\">'upright'</font> (default), <font face=\"courier\">'rotate-left'</font>, or <font face=\"courier\">'rotate-right'</font>.</li>\n</ul> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Referrer Policy: Default to strict-origin-when-cross-origin</h3>\n<p>Web developers may specify a referrer policy on their documents, which impacts the <font face=\"courier\">Referer</font> header sent on outgoing requests and navigations. When no such policy is specified, Chrome <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/6251880185331712\">will now use <font face=\"courier\">strict-origin-when-cross-origin</font> as the default</a> policy, instead of <font face=\"courier\">no-referrer-when-downgrade</font>. On cross-origin requests made from documents without a specified referrer policy, this reduces the <font face=\"courier\">Referer</font> header to the initiating origin.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Update Fallback Content's Behavior for ImageInputType and HTMLImageElement</h3>\n<p>Changes the <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5428567112417280\">behavior of fallback content</a> for <font face=\"courier\">ImageInputType</font> and <font face=\"courier\">HTMLImageElement</font>. Such content will now render exactly the same as alt text would. </p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Update the Behavior of the \"disabled\" Attribute for HTMLLinkElement</h3>\n<p>Corrects <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5110851973414912\">several spec inconsistencies</a> related to the <font face=\"courier\">&lt;link&gt;</font> tag's <font face=\"courier\">disabled</font> attribute.</p>\n<ul>\n <li>Values for the <font face=\"courier\">disabled</font> attribute were not accessible through <font face=\"courier\">document.stylesheets</font>.</li>\n <li>Toggling the <font face=\"courier\">disabled</font> attribute to false then back to true caused it to appear and remain in <font face=\"courier\">document.stylesheets</font>.</li>\n <li>The only way to enable an alternate stylesheet was by disabling, then reenabling it.</li>\n <li>Disabled links were not setting <font face=\"courier\">link.ownerNode</font> to null.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>These behaviors are eliminated in compliance with a <a href=\"https://github.com/whatwg/html/pull/4519\">spec update</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Web Bluetooth writeValueWithResponse() and writeValueWithoutResponse()</h3>\n<p>Adds two new methods, <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5152041850634240\"><font face=\"courier\">writeValueWithResponse()</font> and <font face=\"courier\">writeValueWithoutResponse()</font></a>, which resolve several issues with the existing method for writing to GATT characteristics and enable developers to control whether the device returns a response. The existing <font face=\"courier\">writeValue()</font> method will remain for backwards compatibility, but its use is discouraged. The following problems with the existing method have been corrected:</p>\n<ul>\n <li>It does not allow specifying the type of GATT characteristic write that should be used. This is particularly a problem for devices that support both write types. Writing without response is often desirable for performance reasons, however on most platforms, writing with response is used by default.</li>\n <li>The ability to write with or without response is platform-specific. Currently most platforms prefer writing with a response, but Android prefers writing without a response if both types are available.</li>\n <li>On most platforms, the current implementation depends on the device correctly reporting the available GATT characteristic write types via GATT characteristic properties. If these properties are not set, the characteristic cannot be written to.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The new APIs also do not depend on the GATT characteristic properties being set correctly which allows working around buggy Bluetooth devices.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">WebAssembly BigInt Integration</h3>\n<p>WebAssembly now <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5648655109324800\">imports and exports</a> WebAssembly function parameters of type i64 using BigInt.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">WebAuthn getPublicKey(), getPublicKeyAlgorithm() and getAuthenticatorData()</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5102556109864960\">Several methods</a> from the Web Authentication Level 2 spec have been added. </p>\n<ul>\n <li><font face=\"courier\">getPublicKey()</font> and <font face=\"courier\">getPublicKeyAlgorithm()</font> save sites from parsing Concise Binary Object Representation (CBOR) and CBOR Object Signing and Encryption (COSE) in order to use security keys. CBOR and COSE are somewhat obscure at this time and there's no need for most sites to have to worry about them as the browser is capable of translating them into more standard formats.</li>\n <li><font face=\"courier\">getAuthenticatorData()</font> returns the authenticator data contained within <font face=\"courier\">attestationObject</font>. </li>\n</ul> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">JavaScript</h2>\n<p>This version of Chrome incorporates version 8.1 of the V8 JavaScript engine. It specifically includes the changes listed below. You can find a complete <a href=\"https://v8.dev/blog\">list of recent features</a> in the V8 release notes.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">JavaScript Logical Assignment Operators</h3>\n<p>Adds the logical assignment operators <font face=\"courier\">||=</font>, <font face=\"courier\">&amp;&amp;=</font>, and <font face=\"courier\">??=</font> to JavaScript. This rounds out the compound assignment operators to also include logical binary operators. Currently only mathematical and bitwise binary operators are supported. This improvement is for shipping terser, clearer JavaScript. For more information, see <a href=\"https://v8.dev/features/logical-assignment\">Logical assignment</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Promise.any() and AggregateError</h3>\n<p>Adds <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/5574922384441344\">two new JavaScript features</a> to V8. <font face=\"courier\">Promise.any()</font> accepts an iterable of promises and returns a promise that is fulfilled by the first given promise to be fulfilled, or rejected with an <font face=\"courier\">AggregateError</font> holding the rejection reasons if all of the given promises are rejected. <font face=\"courier\">AggregateError</font> is a support class that aggregates one or more errors into a single object.<br />This rounds out standard JS support for commonly available Promise combinators already available in userland libraries.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">String.prototype.replaceAll()</h3>\n<p>JavaScript now has support for <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/feature/6040389083463680\">global substring replacement</a> through the new <font face=\"courier\">String.prototype.replaceAll()</font> method.</p> \n<h2 style=\"text-align: left;\">Deprecations, and Removals</h2>\n<p>This version of Chrome introduces the deprecations and removals listed below. Visit ChromeStatus.com for lists of <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features#browsers.chrome.status%3A%22Deprecated%22\">current deprecations</a> and <a href=\"https://www.chromestatus.com/features#browsers.chrome.status:%22Removed%22\">previous removals</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">AppCache Removal Begins</h3>\n<p>Chrome 85 starts a spec-mandated turn down of AppCache in Chrome. For details and instructions for managing the transition gracefully, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/appcache-removal/\">Preparing for AppCache removal</a>. For information on a feature that will help you identify uses of this and other deprecated APIs, see <a href=\"https://web.dev/reporting-observer/\">Know your code health</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"text-align: left;\">Reject insecure SameSite=None cookies</h3>\n<p>Use of cookies with <font face=\"courier\">SameSite</font> set to <font face=\"courier\">None</font> without the <font face=\"courier\">Secure</font> attribute is no longer supported.<br />Any cookie that requests <font face=\"courier\">SameSite=None</font> but is not marked Secure will be rejected. This feature started rolling out to users of Stable Chrome on July 14, 2020. See <a href=\"https://www.chromium.org/updates/same-site\">SameSite Updates</a> for a full timeline and details. Cookies delivered over plaintext channels may be cataloged or modified by network attackers. Such </span><a href=\"https://web.dev/user-centric-performance-metrics/#defining-metrics\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">core user experience needs</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> include loading experience, interactivity, and visual stability of page content, and combined are the foundation of the 2020 Core Web Vitals.</span></span></div><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><br /></span></span></div> <a href=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/HlrpevA1hZKx35h2SQdwOBdCO4FOC0YOqie9eMTiGDZx5MdSVTxY2VwPwdL58Pi68cuuG0ooeRTs3RJQEfU5woNRpgq1ZLV4SrWkzHIOH4kTnLS32i62Qf7UibEcz2xm8Gb4nT_e\"><img height=\"180\" src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/HlrpevA1hZKx35h2SQdwOBdCO4FOC0YOqie9eMTiGDZx5MdSVTxY2VwPwdL58Pi68cuuG0ooeRTs3RJQEfU5woNRpgq1ZLV4SrWkzHIOH4kTnLS32i62Qf7UibEcz2xm8Gb4nT_e\" style=\"margin: 0px; height: auto; max-width: 100%;\" /></a> <br /><ul style=\"margin-bottom: 0; margin-top: 0;\"><li><span style=\"color: #1155cc; font-family: inherit; font-size: 11pt; font-weight: 700; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><a href=\"https://web.dev/lcp/\" style=\"text-decoration-line: none;\">Largest Contentful Paint</a></span><span style=\"font-family: inherit; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> measures perceived load speed and marks the point in the page load timeline when the page's main content has likely loaded.</span></li><li><a href=\"https://web.dev/fid/\" style=\"font-family: inherit; font-size: 11pt; text-decoration-line: none; white-space: pre;\"><span style=\"color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-weight: 700; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">First Input Delay</span></a><span style=\"font-family: inherit; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> measures responsiveness and quantifies the experience users feel when trying to first interact with the page.</span></li><li><a href=\"https://web.dev/cls/\" style=\"font-family: inherit; font-size: 11pt; text-decoration-line: none; white-space: pre;\"><span style=\"color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-weight: 700; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Cumulative Layout Shift</span></a><span style=\"font-family: inherit; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> measures visual stability and quantifies the amount of unexpected layout shift of visible page content.</span></li></ul><b style=\"font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><br /></span></b><br /><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span id=\"docs-internal-guid-073a3ec9-7fff-70af-d69f-7092a3d77775\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">All of these metrics capture important user-centric outcomes, are </span><a href=\"https://developers.google.com/web/fundamentals/performance/speed-tools\" style=\"text-decoration-line: none;\"><span style=\"color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">field measurable</span></a><span style=\"font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">, and have supporting lab diagnostic metric equivalents and tooling. For example, while Largest Contentful Paint is the topline loading metric, it is also highly dependent on </span><a href=\"https://web.dev/fcp/\" style=\"text-decoration-line: none;\"><span style=\"color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">First Contentful Paint</span></a><span style=\"font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> (FCP) and </span><a href=\"https://web.dev/time-to-first-byte/\" style=\"text-decoration-line: none;\"><span style=\"color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Time to First Byte</span></a><span style=\"font-size: 11pt; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-variant-numeric: normal; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> (TTFB), which remain critical to monitor and improve.</span></span></span></div><h3 dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 4pt; margin-top: 16pt;\"><span style=\"color: #434343; font-family: inherit; font-size: 14pt; font-weight: 400; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Measuring Core Web Vitals</span></h3><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\">Our goal is to make Core Web Vitals simple and easy to access and measure for all site owners and developers, both across Google surfaces as well as within their own dashboards and tools.</span></span></div><b id=\"docs-internal-guid-c9c343d2-7fff-9a4d-2518-f175a479be1f\" style=\"font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><br /></span></b><br /><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><a href=\"https://developers.google.com/web/tools/chrome-user-experience-report\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Chrome UX Report</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> enables site owners to quickly assess performance of their site for each Web Vital, as experienced by real-world Chrome users. The BigQuery dataset already surfaces publicly accessible histograms for all of the Core Web Vitals, and we are working on a new REST API that will make accessing both URL and origin level data simple and easy — stay tuned.</span></span></div><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><br /></span><br /><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">We strongly encourage all site owners to gather their own </span><a href=\"https://web.dev/user-centric-performance-metrics/#in-the-field\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">real-user measurement analytics</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> for each Core Web Vital. To enable that, a number of browsers, including Google Chrome, support the current Core Web Vitals draft specifications: </span><a href=\"https://wicg.github.io/largest-contentful-paint/\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Largest Contentful Paint</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">, </span><a href=\"https://wicg.github.io/layout-instability/\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Layout Instability</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">, and </span><a href=\"https://wicg.github.io/event-timing/\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">Event Timing</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">. To make it easy for developers to measure Core Web Vitals performance for their sites, today we are launching an open-source </span><a href=\"https://github.com/GoogleChrome/web-vitals/\" style=\"text-decoration: none;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #1155cc; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\">web-vitals</span></a><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"> JavaScript library, which can be used with any analytics provider that supports custom metrics, or as a reference for how to accurately capture each of the Core Web Vitals for your site’s users.</span></span></div></div><br /><br /> <div style=\"background-color: #fafafa;border: solid #e0e0e0 1pt;overflow-wrap: break-word;overflow: hidden;padding: 5pt;max-width: 425px;margin: 0 auto;\"><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: #455a64; font-size: 10pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\">// Example of using web-vitals to measure &amp; report CLS, FID, and LCP.</span></span></div><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\">While today's Core Web Vitals metrics measure three important aspects of user experience on the web, there are many aspects of user experience that are not yet covered by Core Web Vitals. To improve our understanding of user experience going forward, we expect to update Core Web Vitals on an annual basis and provide regular updates on the future candidates, motivation, and implementation status.&nbsp;</span></span></div><b id=\"docs-internal-guid-141029f6-7fff-21da-bf30-b7015eb1d46d\" style=\"font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><br /></span></b><br /><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent; color: black; font-size: 11pt; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: 400; text-decoration: none; vertical-align: baseline; white-space: pre-wrap;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\">Looking ahead towards 2021, we are investing in building better understanding and ability to measure page speed, and other critical user experience characteristics. For example, extending the ability to measure input latency across all interactions, not just the first; new metrics to measure and quantify smoothness; primitives and supporting metrics that will enable delivery of instant and privacy preserving experiences on the web; and more.</span></span></div><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><br /></span><br /><div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"line-height: 1.38; margin-bottom: 0pt; margin-top: 0pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: inherit;\"><span style=\"background-color: transparent;
